  AUTHORS   Pendas AM, Santamaria I, Alvarez MV, Pritchard M and Lopez-Otin C.
  TITLE     Fine physical mapping of the human matrix metalloproteinase genes
            clustered on chromosome 11q22.3
  JOURNAL   Genomics 37 (2), 266-268 (1996)
   PUBMED   8921407
COMMENT     REVIEWED REFSEQ: This record has been curated by NCBI staff. The
            reference sequence was derived from Y12779.1 and AJ296177.1.
            This sequence is a reference standard in the RefSeqGene project.
            On Mar 11, 2004 this sequence version replaced gi:4758724.
            
            Summary: Proteins of the matrix metalloproteinase (MMP) family are
            involved in the breakdown of extracellular matrix in normal
            physiological processes, such as embryonic development,
            reproduction, and tissue remodeling, as well as in disease
            processes, such as arthritis and metastasis. Most MMP's are
            secreted as inactive proproteins which are activated when cleaved
            by extracellular proteinases. The protein encoded by this gene
            degrades amelogenin, the major protein component of dental enamel
            matrix, and thus thought to play a role in tooth enamel formation.
            A mutation in this gene, which alters the normal splice pattern and
            results in premature termination of the encoded protein, has been
            associated with amelogenesis imperfecta. This gene is part of a
            cluster of MMP genes located on chromosome 11q22.3. [provided by
            RefSeq, Aug 2011].
            
            Publication Note:  This RefSeq record includes a subset of the
            publications that are available for this gene. Please see the Gene
            record to access additional publications.

  TITLE     Matrix metalloproteinases

COMMENT     REVIEWED REFSEQ: This record has been curated by NCBI staff. The
            reference sequence was derived from AY358752.1 and BX102293.1.
            On Aug 26, 2005 this sequence version replaced gi:11545845.
            
            Summary: Proteins of the matrix metalloproteinase (MMP) family are
            involved in the breakdown of extracellular matrix in normal
            physiological processes, such as embryonic development,
            reproduction, and tissue remodeling, as well as in disease
            processes, such as arthritis and metastasis. Most MMP's are
            secreted as inactive proproteins which are activated when cleaved
            by extracellular proteinases. [provided by RefSeq, Jul 2008].

COMMENT     REVIEWED REFSEQ: This record has been curated by NCBI staff. The
            reference sequence was derived from DA747742.1, BC057788.1 and
            AK075448.1.
            This sequence is a reference standard in the RefSeqGene project.
            On Jan 29, 2005 this sequence version replaced gi:5174581.
            
            Summary: Proteins of the matrix metalloproteinase (MMP) family are
            involved in the breakdown of extracellular matrix in normal
            physiological processes, such as embryonic development,
            reproduction, and tissue remodeling, as well as in disease
            processes, such as arthritis and metastasis. Most MMP's are
            secreted as inactive proproteins which are activated when cleaved
            by extracellular proteinases. However, the enzyme encoded by this
            gene is activated intracellularly by furin within the constitutive
            secretory pathway. Also in contrast to other MMP's, this enzyme
            cleaves alpha 1-proteinase inhibitor but weakly degrades structural
            proteins of the extracellular matrix. [provided by RefSeq, Jul
            2008].
            
            Transcript Variant: This variant (1) represents the longer
            transcript and encodes the protein.
            
            Publication Note:  This RefSeq record includes a subset of the
            publications that are available for this gene. Please see the Gene
            record to access additional publications.
